Free Talk

"Rotten" or "Rampant"?

—Juan

An article in the April issue of "Literature" aroused Mr. Wu Ai's feelings of "rottenness and rampantness" regarding Westernized literary styles and vocabulary. Taking the opportunity to vent his views, even "mechanism," "contradiction," and "trend" were frowned upon. Mr. Wu Ai then quoted a passage from the Englishman Locke to prove the ridiculousness of people who use such words. In fact, Locke did not say that these words should never be used, but only that they should be used appropriately and appropriately. "Mechanism," "contradiction," and "trend" each have its own special meaning, and there is nothing ridiculous about using them. As long as "the throbbing heartstrings" and "the net of sorrow" are expressed appropriately, it is not a problem if one does not say "Oh, my heartstrings are throbbing!" as soon as one opens one's mouth. The problem with Tianji's joke, "Women burden me like a tumor, children are born like rain, and the tragedy of the petit bourgeoisie is gradually touching us...," is not that it is "too artificial" or "suffers from deliberately writing," but that "a metaphor is inappropriate and the intention is not clear," and it has nothing to do with Westernized literary styles. A child's "being born" will certainly not be "like rain," but the sentence "the tragedy of the petit bourgeoisie is gradually touching us" has no grammatical objection.

I believe that the reason why "the works of many people are filled with words such as "mechanism," "contradiction," and "trend"" is definitely not due to "competing to show off novelty" or "posing coquettishly," let alone because they are "simple in thought" and "afraid that others will think their articles are superficial, so they stubbornly work on the words and sentences to make others find it difficult to understand," nor is it because they "have nothing to say but insist on saying it, so they pinch their throats and pretend," but because the author lacks a more appropriate and more common way of expression, so they have to pick up these words, which make the middle-aged friends who are used to reading thread-bound books have headaches.

Writing in a way that is easy to understand is the right thing to do. But if you can't get more simple and appropriate words, then let's use "mechanism," "contradiction," "trend," "superstructure," and "infrastructure," although they are "difficult to understand," but they are not "unintelligible." "A physically fit woman is also very charming in simple clothes and a cloth skirt," that's right. But if even a "cloth skirt" that is "unique in style" is not available, then just grab some ready-made things (even "foreign goods" are not impossible) to wear. As long as they fit, even if they look "uncomfortable" or "more and more uncomfortable," and even lose the "interest," it is okay, because this can only be blamed on those who watch it being too fond of "comfort" and too fond of the "simple clothes and cloth skirt" that are "unique in style," and have developed a habit, so they feel a little glaring at foreign decorations at a glance.

Didn't Grandmaster Lin feel the entanglement of the "bottom line" and the necessity of advocating quotations because the vernacular used "bottom line" at the same time? I think it is better to continue with the "bottom line." In this regard, my views are somewhat different from Mr. Wu Ai.

Looking at Lianran Painting "Bridge" Notes

— Tang Xiru

I went back to the countryside for the summer last year, which was when the country people were bitterly complaining about the day being dry and the land scorched. The relatively clean water was stored in urns like precious money. Teahouses closed. Drinking tea was restricted. After the washing water was used, it was assigned for washing vegetables or laundry. The river had long been dry. When the peasants running to the lakeside said, "The lake has dried down five or six miles away," there was only a startled bitter smile on people's faces.

At that time, I decided to go down to the lake to take a look. To some extent, I wanted to collect some materials to describe the suffering of the peasants.

I invited my friend Gu Lianran, who likes calligraphy, to go with me.

However, just as our plan was about to be realized, it was immediately dispelled. Many friends advised us not to go. At that time, the peasants had become crazy because of despair. It was easy for us to go there to provoke their anger. They could not tolerate our neat clothes, clean hands, and faces that were not sweating and sun-scorched. They could not tolerate our leisurely attitude and casual mood! "Hey! We are struggling on the line of death, but you are here to watch!" If we were them, we would think so too.

However, a major drought like this is rare to see in my hometown, which is located on the shores of the great Taihu Lake, and has complex waterways. We wanted to leave this painful impression behind as a souvenir. Lianran was determined to paint a picture of the drought. In the end, we found the subject matter almost in the place where we were talking, - the bridges in our small town. At that time, we were surprised when we realized that what we were standing on was the wonderful subject matter we had been looking for for so long! Ah! How many good materials are right in front of us, but are ignored by writers!

We walked to the stone river pier facing the arch of the bridge and squatted down to take a look. The familiar stone bridge had become so strange. It was so high that it was a bit frightening. Because the lower half, which was usually submerged in water, was now completely exposed. The yellow mud riverbed, which originally had only a few green, stinky ponds that had not been sucked dry by the sun, had now increased by more than ten zhang-deep, well-like pools. By separating the mud with straw mats, murky yellow water seeped out. We all thanked the smart people who came up with this idea! Sometimes small smarts can save many people.

People not only fetched water in the riverbed, but many people who walked across the street also no longer relied on this big bridge. A woman secretly released two ducks into the pool to let them swim, but when the two ducks were happily quacking, she immediately picked up the ducks and left, like a frightened mouse.

Lianran spent four or five days painting that bridge. Look at him using yellow, gray, and blue colors. The yellow is the riverbed, and the gray is full of heavy brushstrokes and emotions.

When Lianran was painting, there were usually many townspeople surrounding him to watch every day. On the day he was about to finish painting, it was also the day when the most people were crowding around him. A countryman squeezed in. When he squeezed in and saw what was going on, he immediately squeezed out in disappointment, muttering:

"I thought there was a Western scene to see! It turned out to be like that, some kind of trickery! Can this thing be eaten? Is it worth gathering so many people to watch!"

His words were certainly reckless, but they represented the words of many country farmers! It included a lot of goals and truths for writers. What they need now is "eating." And not anything else. At the same time, I also thought that what we wrote, no matter how proletarian we think it is, is still very, very far away from their lives and needs. Therefore, everyone is the same, first fill your stomach, and then you can fill your brain.

Nagging

— Changmin

—Written in dialect

You fellow really don't know what's good for you,

A string of words that can't be chewed,

As smelly and long as Wang Mama's foot wraps.

A frog jumps in an oil lamp,

The cowhide roars, blowing up a storm.

I see you're really incorrigibly poor,

Eating porridge and pouring in vegetable soup!

Quickly shut your big mouth,

Lest the mirror reflect the face of a twisted-mouth shrew.

I say these days are like rats biting cow horns,

The tighter the bite, the less hope.

Last year, the weather was good and the crops were abundant,

Hoping to fill the stomachs of the whole family;

Who knew that the sky would have unpredictable storms, and disaster would come out of nowhere,

Everyone was happy like sparrows in coarse chaff.

Alas, we are all turtledoves in the bamboo forest,

Not knowing spring and autumn, not understanding the situation;

Well, like dogs biting mosquitoes, we can only let life collide with fate!

University Days (I)

— By German writer Storm, translated by Chen Yin

Nali

I didn't have a sister, so no one introduced me to girls of the same age to make friends. But I went to dance lessons. Dance lessons were twice a week, and the location was at the city government ten; the city hall was also the city's residential area. The mayor's son was my Bingming; they together had eight, Guo jump without, city level, students full in the car. However, when it came to five dance partners, a door problem that was difficult to solve initially arose: an eighth female dance partner of equal status could not be found.

But the mayor's son, Fritz, had a solution. There was a woman who used to work as a mother at his home, and the mayor still asks her to help when there are banquets. She married a tailor who tailored old clothes, a skinny, yellow-faced man with a French surname who liked to talk big in the hotel more than to pick up a needle and thread and work at the tailor's desk. This family lives on those streets at the end of the city facing the palace park. That little tree, that ten-tree dam is similar to them. The door of this tree almost completely blocks the only window. We often pass by in front of that house, wanting to take a glimpse of that lovely little girl: she often likes to sit behind a few pots of sweet osmanthus and canary grass and sew things, and she actually occupies a very important place in our childhood fantasies.

She is the only child of a French tailor, a beautiful thirteen-year-old girl, and although the clothes she wears are made of ordinary materials, her mother keeps her very clean. Her light brown skin and dark eyes indicate that her father is of foreign descent. I still remember that she combs her black hair very low, all the way to the side of her temples, which makes her originally small face even more charming.

No Father

— Chen Fuxi

Qiu'er has no father.

Father is dead. But Qiu'er doesn't know what death is. When his father died, he saw his mother crying, his sister crying, so he cried too. He didn't know why he was crying, he just felt that crying was fun. Usually, if he woke up and didn't see his mother, he would cry; if he saw something he wanted to eat but didn't buy it, he would also cry; or if the children next door beat him, he would also cry; and when he cried, tears would flow down his face, as if he had unspeakable suffering. When his father died, Qiu'er didn't shed tears, he just learned to wail like his mother, and after wailing a few times, he laughed.

"Mom, Dad is sleeping, Dad..."

He twisted his mother's clothes and said. But his mother ignored him and just kept crying. Qiu'er found it strange: why was Mom always crying at Dad? He was a five-year-old child, who could just run and talk, and didn't understand anything. Someone put mourning clothes on him, that white linen clothes, white shoes, white hat, which made Qiu'er even more puzzled: he saw his mother, sister, and brother, all wearing white. He thought in his little belly: wearing white clothes probably meant going to the streets to play; because in the past, whenever Mom and Dad took him to see a play, they would always change into new clothes. Therefore, after he put on the mourning clothes, he could hardly stand still, fearing that Mom and sister wouldn't go with him, and murmured:

"Let's go see, go to the streets..." No one paid attention to him as he made such a fuss. Qiu'er was really pitiful, he didn't understand anything. When he slowly grew up, he never saw his biological father. In his mind, he never knew that he had a father. One sunny afternoon, Qiu'er ran to the neighbor's house to play and saw that A Mao had a white rubber dog, chocolate candy, and a brand new, fun toy car. As long as you wound the spring, the car would start on the smooth ground. Qiu'er was very happy to see this toy car and couldn't wait to take it back from A Mao's house immediately. What he usually saw were huge cars, but Qiu'er had never seen such a delicate, novel toy car before. Now that he saw it suddenly, he felt frustrated because he loved it but couldn't get it. He really wanted to have one himself. He wanted to ask A Mao for it, but he couldn't bring himself to ask, knowing that A Mao would definitely not give it away. He thought it would be nice to borrow it to play with, so he mumbled a request to A Mao:

"Can you let me play with this toy car?"

"Sure."

Having received A Mao's permission, Qiu'er took it in his hand and wound the spring. Before long, the car really started on the smooth cement floor. Qiu'er was envious and played with it again and again. Finally, he asked:

"A Mao, who bought this for you?"

"My dad."

"Dad?"

Hearing the two words "Dad", Qiu'er was stunned. He thought to himself: why don't I have a dad? Where is my dad? Why doesn't he buy me a toy car? Qiu'er knew A Mao's dad. He was a man who wore glasses and Western clothes, and who often hugged A Mao and kissed him, but he didn't understand why he didn't have a dad.

He went home with a melancholy mood.

"Mom, do I have a dad?" Qiu'er asked.

"Of course you do!"

"Then where is my dad?"

"You'll know when you grow up."

Qiu'er was at a loss. During the Cold Food Festival, the family went to the countryside to sweep the tombs. Mom pointed to a green tomb that looked like a steamed bun and said:

"Your dad is inside here..."

He seemed to understand a little, but he didn't understand clearly. He still didn't understand what death was, and thought that his dad would come home one day, so the next day, when he met A Mao, he said to A Mao:

"I have a dad too."

Saying that, Qiu'er laughed happily. It was as if his dad was also going to buy him a brand new, delicate toy car.

White Spirit Temple (Continued)

— Yuan Chenying

Behind the Mongolian yurt stood the "Obo" mountain, with several people gazing into the distance. I slowly walked up, powerless. The mountain wasn't high. Looking ahead from the Obo: It was a vast, flat grassland. A cold wind blew from the north, and large patches of white clouds floated in the blue sky. Looking at the boundless land ahead, I suddenly thought that if a large troop of Mongolian soldiers on Mongolian horses were galloping across it, the scene would certainly be heroic and martial.

After descending the hillside, our boys had all gone to the temple fair, leaving me alone and forlorn in the yurt. A feeling of desolation and loneliness suddenly overwhelmed me. I walked out of the yurt, passed through the rows of yurts, and headed east towards the river.

Emerging from beside the yurts piled high with cow dung (Note 2), the air was still. Only a few pedestrians crossed the single-plank bridge. When I passed by, they merely glanced at me and then walked towards the yurts, speaking Mongolian that I couldn't understand.

Across the river were some earthen houses at the foot of the mountain, about twenty or so. Walking through an alleyway piled with garbage, a dog lay there quietly. Around the bend was a newly opened restaurant. The sound of stir-frying came from inside. A red paper sign on the window read: "No Credit." Wanting to drink something, I walked in, unexpectedly hearing a familiar voice:

"Hey! When did you get here?"

I looked up in surprise at the kang (Note 3) and saw Mr. H, whom I knew from Guihua City, greeting me.

"I arrived yesterday! What a coincidence, meeting you here." I said, sitting on the kang, as if meeting a relative in a foreign land.

Mr. H poured me a cup of tea. I asked him when he had arrived and what he was doing here. He lowered his head and quietly told me that he had been here for four or five days, trying to find a job. He hadn't expected that there were so many people here already, too many! There was no way to find a position, and he would probably have to go back… Then he sighed and said, "Too many people, not enough jobs," it's like that everywhere! Even this Mongolian place has unemployment. These earthen houses are full of officials from the Mongolian Political Council and people who came here hoping to find a job at the Mongolian Political Council!

After eating a few sentences, Mr. H and I walked out of the restaurant. He pointed me to the post office and bid me farewell. I walked into the post office alone.

The post office was in an earthen house without a courtyard wall. The stove was burning brightly, and a clerk was preparing to cook. I talked with the postmaster and learned that letters were delivered by horse courier, three times a month. He was from Beiping and said that life here was very hard. No matter spring, summer, autumn, or winter, there were no vegetables to eat. Only the postman occasionally brought some vegetables from the city… He only stopped talking when I said goodbye.

Walking out of the post office, thinking about Mr. H's words and the postmaster's complaints, I couldn't help but feel lost in this Mongolian land.

Note 1: "Camel hair quilt" is made of camel hair, filled with camel hair, extremely warm, and used by the people of Suiyuan to keep warm.

Note 2: The cow dung piled in front of the Mongolian yurt is used by the Mongolians for cooking fires.

Note 3: "Kang" In the north, earthen kangs are used as beds. "Kang shang" means on the bed, as southerners would say.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Conversations

A Discussion on Preventing Suicide

— Hen

In recent years, the trend of suicide has been increasing daily. According to statistics from this city for the past year, one person commits suicide every four hours. The alarming number is already an obstacle to the nation's future. Recently, it has become even more severe, with entire families committing suicide together, the tragic harm of which threatens to destroy the nation. Discussing methods of prevention is truly the most urgent and pressing task at hand. Reading Director Wu's opinion on preventing suicide, the argument is concise and essential, and the benevolent words are widely beneficial, worthy of being called a good medicine for saving the times. I will add some supplements to Director Wu's three points, as a small contribution.

Regarding psychological transformation, in addition to Director Wu's point that newspapers and films should do their best to avoid sensationalizing suicides and refrain from sympathy, more emphasis should be placed on educational enlightenment, establishing a common goal. Citizens are the essential elements of a national organization. Destroying oneself is destroying the nation. Encourage their will to strive upward and the true value of life. At this time of promoting literacy education, the opportunity can be used to attack the evils of suicide, providing a strong remedy for the general uneducated population. Furthermore, in various supplementary schools and women's schools, instill students with a spirit of struggle. In ordinary primary and secondary schools, emphasis should be placed on production education and vocational skills, breaking the misconception of simply burying oneself in books, in order to cope with the current economic difficulties.

Regarding substantial assistance, this city only has one municipal poor people's loan office to help the common people, which is far too few. It is truly necessary to expand the organization and establish branch offices in different districts. At the same time, improve the small loan methods of the banking sector. Because nowadays, if common people have urgent needs and go to the bank for loans, there are many difficulties. Even if the loan is successfully obtained, they have already tasted countless hardships. I believe that bank loans, in order to guarantee property rights, only need to investigate whether the borrower has a skill and whether there is a guarantor, and the transaction can be completed. There should be no intentional delays to cause embarrassment. Therefore, the level of substantial assistance should require banks to improve their methods and expand the poor people's loan capital, so as to facilitate turnover.

Regarding improving relief efforts, according to the situation in this city, people tend to focus on the dead and neglect the living. Even if it cannot be said that personal connections are used in charitable affairs, the fact that the truly poor cannot obtain benefits is indeed a fact. For the sake of the present, the authorities should pay attention to various charitable organizations, strictly supervise them, and transform charitable organizations that distribute benefits into profit-generating organizations. The method is to start with investigation, with the authorities appointing people to improve the content of all public and private charitable organizations by districts, making them industrialized groups. All applicants for relief should be required to enter the organization to learn crafts, using their earned wages to support their lives. If there is a surplus, half goes to the public and half goes to private ownership, so that the unemployed have jobs and the lazy are motivated, as a large-scale reform to eliminate the previous organizations that were solely for distributing benefits and encouraging dependence. (With compliments)

Lamp

— Tan Tan

The weather is gradually getting hotter. At night, although there is some wind, everything in the room has been baked hot by the sun all day. Therefore, the time I fall asleep at night has to be delayed day by day. Recently, I don't even dare to turn on the electric light much, because its heat, although not very high, gives me a considerable sense of annoyance in my senses with its incandescent light.

Regarding lamps, I actually like them very much. If someone asked me, "What do you like most in the world?" then I would definitely answer without hesitation, "I like lamps the most."

I don't know what I felt when I first saw a lamp after being born from my mother's body. I guess I was surprised by everything at that time, so I wouldn't pay special attention to the lamp. But after I had memories, the lamp gave me a good impression, which is very clear.

I don't know if it was when I was six or seven years old, I didn't sleep in the same bed with my mother anymore. In winter, the night is very long, and I go to bed early, so I often wake up at one or two o'clock. That was when my mother and the others had been asleep for a long time and were sleeping soundly. Although I called out in a tender voice, they couldn't hear me much. At this time, I felt terrified. It was as if everyone in the family had run away, leaving only me. Just as I was about to cry, I saw an oil lamp on a small table in front of my bed through the printed cotton mosquito net. At that time, the wick had been turned down very low, and it wasn't glaring even when looking closely. I immediately felt warmth and peace of mind, like finding a relative, and fell asleep again. Even now, the scene at that time is still vividly in my mind, especially the layer of haze on the transparent lampshade due to the kerosene fumes!

When I was fifteen or sixteen years old, I had already developed a very natural habit of reading at night. For a better book, it was common to read until three or four in the morning. Because I read at night, my father specially bought me a kerosene lamp with a white lampshade. It was taller and larger than ordinary kerosene lamps. The wick of ordinary kerosene lamps is a tongue-shaped strip, while this one is a circular shape; therefore, its light is two or three times stronger than that of ordinary oil lamps. At that time, I had no experience of reading under electric lights, so when I lit it, I felt that the whole room was bright and my eyes were clear and my heart was happy. Especially interesting was that this kind of lamp also had a frame made of thick lead wire or something similar, and there was also a small brass hook on the frame. When lit at night, I could boil water on the lamp to brew tea, or warm up some cooked lotus seeds and lilies. I didn't really want to eat anything at night,

Page 18

but I really wanted to drink good tea, so the brass hook often made pleasant sounds on the lamp frame. What made me especially happy was that on several snowy nights, after I finished reading a volume of books, I carried the small hook outside to the water tank to fetch water. When I got closer, I saw that the water in the tank had frozen into ice, and a layer of snow had been added on top of the ice. I didn't hesitate to use the lead spoon that always left water, put the snow on the ice in the brass hook, and boiled it on the lamp. When it boiled, I brewed it and drank it, and it tasted several times better than usual.

The Lantern Festival is the Lantern Festival, but in our hometown, the lanterns are hung up from New Year's Eve. One year, also because of my special love for lamps, I hung twenty-four red gauze lanterns on the corridors on all sides of the 口-shaped house in my home. At the same time, six pairs of candles with bright horn covers were burned in the inner hall. At that time, the adults were all preparing the necessary things for the New Year in the house, and I was the only one who was responsible for guarding the middle of the courtyard. Although the house was not magnificent, I felt that it was quite luxurious.

Speaking of red gauze lanterns, I remembered another thing. That year, it was my relative's sister's wedding, and I was ordered to attend the wedding banquet. I have never liked drinking the wine of women, because as soon as the bridal sedan chair leaves, it seems unbearably lonely. This time, there was no way, I had to go. At the same time, the person getting married was also very close to me. Under these circumstances, I naturally had no choice but to drink with my throat. Sure enough, it wasn't long before I was so drunk that I couldn't stand up straight.

When the relatives saw that I was drunk, they called two servants to help me home. My house and my relatives' house were separated by a rather deserted street, with few street lights. All the lanterns in their house had been taken out for serious business. They had no choice but to take off a hanging red gauze lantern and hand it to a smaller servant. I leaned on the shoulder of the larger servant, and a red gauze lantern led the way, slowly returning home. At that time, the long street was deserted, and the crescent moon was beautiful. Although I was drunk, I felt inexplicably happy. All the way, I murmured the two sentences "The sound of pipes and flutes returns to the courtyard, the lights go down the tower." In fact, the ten-tune music of the relatives' family was coming in waves!

Flood

— Xiaoyun

"This annoying weather, always drizzling rain, it's really going to kill us poor people! ... Alas, in this kind of weather, who would want to eat cold noodles?" Old Zhang Fa got up early in the morning, looked at the gray sky in the courtyard, and the thin, long raindrops like cold noodle money in front of the eaves. His chest felt as if it had been pierced by a poisonous arrow, and he muttered to himself in secret.

Old Zhang Fa was an old man about fifty or sixty years old, with a bald head, a hunched back, dark skin, and many deep wrinkles deeply imprinted on his forehead, like the rings of a tree, recording the hardships of his life. Every year, in addition to planting more than a dozen acres of dry land at the entrance of the village to barely maintain the family's food, after the work in the fields was finished, if he could get a little free time, he and his son would do seasonal small businesses, earning a little profit to help the family's expenses. For example, now it is the hot month of May, so he makes cold noodles, carrying the burden, selling them back and forth in the village.

"Dad - Dad - the situation out ... side ... side is really a bit bad! This morning I passed by the stream in front of the village, and the water rose so fast that it was almost overflowing the embankment, and it was as turbid as mud!" His eldest son, A Gen, came in from the outside carrying a burden, his clothes all soaked by the rain, and strings of water droplets dripped from under the hem of his pants. Panting, he said that there was no business at all today, and he walked through two villages without earning a cent! Just now he passed by Uncle Zhi Xiang's door, and Uncle Zhi Xiang was urging his son to move the goods in the store, he said: "This time the stream water is rising very badly, and it is so rapid, it has not been seen in more than ten years. I think the mountain torrents above are not small!" Dad, I think, this time we can't avoid a flood!" His son, A Gen, said as he carried the burden under the window by the door.

Old Zhang Fa unconsciously raised his head to look at the sky outside the window, sighed a long breath, lowered his head, and sat back on the edge of the bed, silently smoking his dry tobacco.

"Dad, our place is also low-lying, we should prepare first, otherwise, when the flood comes, there won't be enough time to move the things in the house." He began to pull out the broken wooden box with a missing ear from under the bed.

Old Zhang Fa was still silent and did not say a word, his head lower than before. He thought of the dozen acres of dry land at the entrance of the village, the dry land bearing fat rice! He kept imagining that after the flood, wouldn't the rice fields be ruined by the flood? At that time, the autumn harvest would be hopeless, so where would the family's food and clothing be raised? Thinking of this, it seemed that a grimacing demon was standing in front of him, stretching out its furry giant arm, groping for his head. He was so frightened that goosebumps appeared all over his body, and he dared not imagine it any further.

"Alas! Since Heaven doesn't want to keep people alive, there's no place to escape to even if we run!" Old Zhang Fa hummed in a drawn-out voice.

The rain in the courtyard was getting heavier and heavier, and the rainwater in front of the eaves was flowing淙淙潺潺.

Suddenly, a gong sound came from the village, along with a noisy and chaotic sound.

"Everyone come out to help guard the embankment, the embankment is about to collapse!"

Not long after this sound passed, there was a loud "哗..." sound from outside the village, clearly the embankment had been breached by the stream torrent.

"Run for your life! ... Run for your life quickly!" A mournful cry came in!

"Dad, let's run, let's run quickly! If we're late..." His son hurried over to help his father.

"Child, where can we run to? ..."

Love and Desire

— Xinlu

It is the season when peonies are in bloom.

Stepping into the imperial garden, Dong Xiaowan's heart kept pounding. She lowered her head, only caring about shrinking into her chest; her eyes were on the ground, almost closing her eyelids in fear. The faint sweat that seeped out of her forehead made her suspect that she was rolling around in a steamer.

On the one hand, she was concerned that her husband, Mao Pijiang, who had sneaked into the palace disguised as a eunuch, would be discovered by the Yongzheng Emperor if he stayed here for too long; on the other hand, she felt an undeniable sense of guilt and shame. Wasn't it the case? She had originally agreed with him to elope on Qingming Festival, but now? The Dragon Boat Festival had also passed long ago, but she was still attached to the deep palace. The secret words of vows made in the past had all turned into empty bubbles. Although the palace guards were strict, making it difficult to act for a while, her own lack of courage, her refusal to tear down the fortress of love between her and the Yongzheng Emperor, her determination to fly out of his arms, was ultimately an ironclad fact. This made her conscience suffer severe condemnation, and her nerves twitched with pain, as if a frightened bird's iron claws were hooking her soul.

"Heavens! If you don't save me again, I will be tormented to death by this contradictory life!" She sighed softly, comfortably stretching her right wrist out of the Yongzheng Emperor's embrace, and slightly raised her eyes to look over, already seeing her husband, Mao Pijiang, kneeling to welcome her in front of the Nine Dragon Pavilion.

"What's wrong? Xiaowan!"

"Your Majesty, I feel that life is ultimately just a short tragedy. When the source of life has spilled the last drop, who can avoid shaking hands and turning into dust; the passion, love, and desire of life all return to the void in fragments. How can it not make people feel frustrated!"

"Ah, Xiaowan, why are you always so sentimental? Your distress also causes me endless pain; people are just people after all! Xiaowan, please don't think wildly anymore! Look at how luxuriantly the peonies are blooming, let's have three drinks." The Yongzheng Emperor clung tightly

nestled up to her, with a slight moistness in his eyes, and truly loved her, giving her boundless sympathy and tenderness; she was so grateful that she was almost crying.

The sound of light footsteps startled the little sparrows in the trees, and they chirped and flew away, and the entire space fell into a deathly silence.

Entering the Nine Dragon Pavilion, the banquet had already been set. Mao Pijiang stood respectfully by the side, serving; his face was even thinner than before. Dong Xiaowan felt great pity in her heart, thinking that he was originally a scholarly gentleman who was accustomed to being pampered, but because he was unwilling to have his wife taken away, he had traveled and struggled and suffered all the pain in the world. Now I am enjoying myself and drinking wine above, but he is flattering at the bottom of the steps, which can't help but make her feel a strong burst of bitterness:

"Ah"!

"Ah"!

Crabapple Jade Cup,

Zhilan Fish,

Dragon Liver Meat,

……

……

Objects were shaking in front of her, one ten, a thousand… She威到 her head was strangely light, the sky seemed to be collapsing, she looked at Yongzheng, looked at Mao Pijiang, their faces were all terribly stupid, a dreamlike illusion expanded, big, big… as big as a cloud felt, holding her straight up, she seemed to be walking on the wind in the air, and in a flash she fell into the peony flower bushes, the crimson color made her feel the fear of her future destiny, and it seemed that Yongzheng's face became hideous and terrifying, gradually he opened his bloody mouth and wanted to devour her. She hurriedly ran to Mao Pijiang for help, but unexpectedly, Mao Pijiang also held a steel knife and rushed at her fiercely from the opposite side. She fled to the side for her life. Suddenly, the sky was dark and the earth was dark, and countless black shadows stopped her way, just as she was about to be killed, the steel knife had already struck straight down from behind, and she cried and fell down with a wail.

"Wake up"!

"Wake up"!

The sunlight suddenly dimmed, the sky was so gloomy that it made people

shiver, the bees were buzzing, and the peonies seemed to

became dark purple.

Mangzhong (Grain in Ear)

— Xinye

"In the countryside, there are few idle people in April, as they have just finished sericulture and are preparing the paddy fields"; in the countryside, April in the lunar calendar is simply the busiest season for farmers, and at the same time, it is also the most hopeful and precious season. At this time, regardless of men, women, and children, everyone has their work to do: especially in the rural areas of Jiangnan, after the tea and silkworm matters are over, the flower and fruit fields come next; as long as it waits for a little water to come in Small Fullness, everyone must soak the grain seeds and make the seedling fields, and when it is near Mangzhong, everyone must prepare to transplant the seedlings.

Uncle A Shun got up early this morning, and he went to the pillar to take down that "Yinyang He Li Tong Shu" to read: although he did not know many characters, but the blind man reading long lines, even more so, the major and minor solar terms of the year were familiar to him. He turned to April:

"M! April is small, May is big, the 20th of April is Small Fullness, and the 7th of May is Grain in Ear. Although the Small Fullness water does not come, the grain seeds must always be soaked. There is not a grain of our own grain seeds left, and Yinnan still has a lot, so let's go and discuss it with him first, and borrow a dozen or twenty catties to soak it and then talk about it." He thought to himself, then closed the almanac and hung it back in its original place, then sat down on the doorstep with a butt, looked up at the sky, the sky was so cloudy, but it didn't rain. He picked up the tide cigarette holder, desperately sucking, as if to solve many problems in this smoking!

"Last year, the water in the outer part of Zhihe Tou, the Lingdangzi, was small, so we didn't plant water chestnuts, and later changed to planting indica rice. Although we ate many hardships that we had never experienced before, we still received more than eight stone of steamed grain rice. But, but this year's water is even smaller, and many pieces of mud are protruding outside: although the water chestnut seeds have been sown, don't think there will be water chestnuts to pick. Even the indica rice, I'm afraid, won't have any hope!" His wife had just dressed the little Mao, who was only a week old, from the room, and when she heard her man mention the matter of soaking the grain seeds, she babbled like this as she walked to the stove door to ask. Uncle A Shun did not reply, but continued to smoke the tide cigarette, and his eyes were fixed on the messy stones in the courtyard. Suddenly, a spider hung down from the eaves and happened to fall on his forehead. He slapped it with his hand, and a bubble of liquid burst out. He looked at his palm, and the innocent little spider had turned into a meat paste, so he wiped the dirt on his hands on his straw shoes, but continued to think about his concerns in his heart:

"If the Dang fields can't be planted, dreaming of planting in the mountain fields is impossible...? The water in the river is only a foot deep, and this year won't be better than last year! The source of water will be cut off in the future..." His wife interrupted and said:

"But it's not okay not to plant, everyone else is transplanting seedlings, and we can't let a few fields be empty, we have to try our luck, maybe the Small Fullness water doesn't come, but the yellow plum water will come sooner or later."

"It's already too late when the yellow plum water comes, and the seedlings in the fields can be burned as firewood!"

"It's always better than not coming at all, it's always better to have something to salvage."

"Never mind, let's soak the grain first!" He said weakly, and went to Yinnan with a bamboo basket to borrow grain seeds.

After borrowing fifteen catties of japonica rice grains, he carefully walked to the river to wash it clean, and floated out all the floating grains, filled a light crock with clean water, and poured all the basket of wool grains into it, and then pressed it in the corner of the courtyard.

He silently ate breakfast, and carried a hoe and iron harrow to the Hengtian Tou to make a seedling field; his wife was at home sorting out silkworm-raising furniture;

"Hey! We haven't raised silkworms, but it's still the same as doing housework." She said to herself.

They raised a season of silkworms, but did not see a silkworm cocoon, and now their lives for a year must be entrusted to the autumn harvest in the future; what was borrowed before, what is eaten now, and what will be needed in the future, must all wait for the autumn harvest to compensate. But the impression given to him in front of him is too bad; so that this distant, vague hope, finally sinks in an invisible, untouchable abyss!

Amateur Mailbox

The Difference Between Envoys and Ambassadors

In the past half-month, countries such as Britain, the United States, Germany, and Japan have successively promoted their envoys to China to the rank of ambassador. However, many general readers are unclear about the distinction between "envoy" and "ambassador," so we have received numerous inquiries in recent days. In addition to replying to each letter separately, the editor believes it is necessary to provide a public explanation and will summarize the differences below:

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

According to current international practice, diplomatic representatives are divided into four ranks: first-class ambassadors, second-class envoys, third-class ministers resident, and fourth-class chargés d'affaires. Heads of missions to major powers are always ambassadors, while only envoys are sent to countries of secondary importance. This is because an ambassador represents the monarch or head of state, while an envoy represents the government. The rank of ambassador is one level higher than that of envoy, and in terms of international protocol, sending an ambassador is naturally much more courteous. Furthermore, an ambassador can directly and promptly meet with diplomatic authorities and request an audience with the head of state. This offers certain advantages in diplomatic communication or when dealing with specific negotiations. In countries such as Britain and the United States, it is very difficult for envoys from secondary countries to gain an audience with the foreign minister of the host country. One must send in a request well in advance, and if the minister is unavailable, only a director, counselor, or deputy minister may be available for a meeting. In terms of protocol and diplomatic relations, this is naturally inferior to having an ambassador. Britain, the United States, France, Italy, Germany, and Japan all exchange ambassadors because they are all major powers and therefore treat each other as equals. However, they treat China differently. China has always been looked down upon by other countries. With the exception of Russia, which resumed diplomatic relations with China after its revolution and exchanged ambassadors, the heads of mission of other countries stationed in China were still envoys, treating China as a country of secondary importance. This is truly a humiliation! Not long ago, Italy was the first to promote its head of mission to China to the rank of ambassador, and in the past month, Britain, the United States, Germany, and Japan have also successively elevated their heads of mission in China. On the surface, it seems that they have all recognized China as a major power, which is worth celebrating. However, we must understand that the promotion of the heads of mission to China by the major powers is not the result of China's own increased strength but a kind of diplomatic maneuver in the international arena. We should take advantage of this international situation, rouse ourselves, and strive to achieve genuine equality in both name and reality, so that China can obtain truly equal treatment. This is the understanding that the general public should have regarding the changes in relations between the various countries and China.

The editor has always prioritized individual replies in this column, as readers are well aware. Due to space constraints in the future, only questions that are of particular relevance to the general public will be answered in the newspaper; other inquiries will only be answered by letter. To avoid misunderstandings, this is hereby clarified.

Shen Bao This City Supplement Automotive Weekly

Overview of the British Automotive Industry in the First Four Months of This Year

— Shadow Stay

(1) Amazing Domestic Market Records The British automotive industry has made significant progress in recent years, and this year in particular has been booming. The number of private cars produced broke all previous British records in the first quarter. In the first four months of this year, the number of new car registrations increased from 66,824 in the same period last year to 83,866. Not only passenger cars but also trucks saw a similar increase in registrations, from 22,514 in the same period last year to 24,612 this year. If we further analyze the registration figures by horsepower, large cars have also clearly increased. The number of new cars with 25 horsepower or more registered this year increased by half compared to the same period last year. However, in fact, most of the new cars currently being manufactured by British factories are not around 25 horsepower but small 10-horsepower cars. At the same time, we can also note that the environment for the British automotive industry has improved because the car horsepower tax has been significantly reduced. The increase in the number of high-horsepower cars is naturally due to this reason.

(2) Sharp Increase in Overseas Market Sales The British car market had considerable development in the domestic market in the first four months of this year, as mentioned above, but at the same time, the overseas market has also developed similarly. In particular, large cars and high-horsepower vehicles have made considerable progress in exports recently. In recent months, Hooper, a well-known London car body manufacturer, has shipped many new car bodies overseas and is currently working hard to prepare to deliver the orders it has received one after another. Countries such as India, Australia, Spain, Turkey, Romania, Hungary, and Switzerland have all ordered large quantities of car bodies from the factory. Most of these car bodies are equipped with Rolls-Royce chassis. A particularly large car body, mounted on a 40-50 horsepower Rolls-Royce chassis, was recently completed and delivered to the President of the West Indian Republic. In fact, this can be considered an armored car because it is covered in bulletproof steel plates and glass. Even so, the weight of the entire car is only five times heavier than an ordinary car.

(3) Good Performance in Car Races In recent years, British cars have not only made considerable progress in sales but have also clearly improved in engineering compared to the past. We can get some evidence from the results of the races alone. Recently, a Duke Gobel drove a "Qingdao" brand car again to participate in a car race in Daddonay and achieved an amazing record. Therefore, he won general recognition that the "Qingdao" brand car is a number of cars. During the competition, there was also an old 10-horsepower, two-cylinder Rolls-Royce car manufactured in 1904-05. This old car is owned by the South Kai-Deng Place Science Museum. Although it is 30 years old, the competition results showed a very good performance. The facts tell us that not only have the recent products of British cars achieved amazing results, but even old cars have considerable achievements.

(4) On-Site Test of Lubricating Oil Recently, a famous scientist, Mr. Lu Ai, conducted an on-site test of lubricating oil in Brockland to prove which method of using lubricating oil is the best and which lubricating oil can travel longer. Using the products of the Qier Mu Oil Company, under the guidance of Mr. Lu Ai, the specified lubricating oil was used up and tested on-site once. During the test, two identical 1935 Austin cars were used to travel 550 miles and then stopped. The results showed that the inside of the cylinder, in addition to leaving a thin film, had no remaining oil. Calculated by speed, the car traveled 30 miles per hour. One new car used the best lubricating oil to accelerate and stopped after traveling 9.6 miles. The other car used Qier Mu Oil and stopped after traveling 16 miles. Therefore, the facts have told us that sufficient lubricating oil can make acceleration powerful, and the driving time of the vehicle can also be longer.

(5) Ascension Memorial and the Automotive Industry The entire month of May in England was a celebration of the 25th anniversary of King George's ascension to the throne and was very lively. People from all over England flocked to London to see the excitement, and even overseas tourists took this opportunity to arrive by boat in batches. As a result, hotels declared that they were fully booked, and the waiters in the restaurants were yelling that the dishes were sold out. All kinds of lively situations are naturally endless. The automotive business is no exception. The number of cars in London has increased sharply due to the increased number of tourists from all over the country driving to London. The business of taxis and public buses has increased threefold, which proves that the automotive business has benefited from the King's Ascension Memorial. Undoubtedly, many tourists need cars when they stay in London. Maybe they will buy a new car to take back when they leave London. Therefore, car dealers in London have displayed a large number of new cars in their showrooms. Vauxhall cars with 12-14 horsepower have branch offices in London. These vehicles are very popular with tourists. The 1934 Vauxhall car had amazing results. Old cars are also quite active in the market, and there are many tourists who buy and sell them.

(6) Extreme Attention to Road Problems Under this situation, traffic in England has become increasingly congested. Therefore, a group of road authorities have had to pay extra attention to road safety plans to bring the country's roads to the most economical and safest limits. The most important issue at present is how to make the cost of road construction the most economical and the most durable in the future. According to the research results of British road scientists, the road building material must be hard. In terms of pressure, each square inch can withstand 200 pounds of force. The surface is covered with a layer of small stones. The fine bumps on the road surface must be removed. It must not only be glossy but also non-slip. This will naturally increase the safety problem. The repair of old roads and the opening of new roads are currently being actively carried out by British road authorities. The results of the road construction movement will directly and indirectly promote the automotive business.

A Collection of New Automotive News

— Yu

Advocating Car Tax Revenue for Highways: The American Road Builders' Association and Highway Exhibition recently held its 32nd annual meeting in Washington. Attending were highway officials, engineers, contractors, and manufacturers from various cities and states, totaling no fewer than 5,000 people. At the time, the assembly advocated that all national gasoline taxes and car license fees should be used for road construction in various states, instead of being used for emergency relief or other purposes. Highway officials stated: Currently, various states are diverting this tax revenue for other purposes, amounting to no less than US$200,000,000 annually. If this continues, the future of highways is in danger, and it will inevitably lead to various states being unable to participate in the expenditure of federal highway projects. The main advocacy in the meeting was to continue with complete road design planning, with all road tax revenue being used for road administration. Federal road construction funding must also continue to be allocated as before.

Scheduled Completion of the American Automobile Bridge: The automobile bridge between San Francisco and Oakland is scheduled to be completed in December 1936. This bridge is divided into upper and lower layers, specifically for automobile traffic. Driving from the Oakland end towards the bridge, one first passes a wide tree-lined avenue, one and a quarter miles long. After passing the toll booth, one easily ascends to the upper layer, traveling 19,000 feet to Yerba Buena Island in the middle. After passing this island, there are four huge towers, reaching the two-mile road at the western end. Traveling another mile reaches the San Francisco terminus. Trucks travel on the lower level of the bridge. Except for the 3,000 feet crossing Yerba Buena Island, the western side is traversed by huge tunnels. The entire bridge is divided into two layers to ensure the balance of automobile driving. The upper level has six lanes, and the lower level has five lanes. Among them, three lanes are for trucks, and the other two lanes are for streetcar tracks. The tree-lined avenue on the upper level is ten feet wide per lane, divided into two speed categories. The four middle lanes allow speeds of 45 to 55 miles per hour, while the two outer lanes allow speeds of 30 to 45 miles per hour. According to expert estimates, in the first year of the bridge's completion and opening, namely 1937, approximately 8,000,000 vehicles will pass through. In 1943, it will be 10,000,000 vehicles. In 1950, it will be 12,500,000 vehicles. However, an average of 30,000,000 vehicles can pass through annually without any congestion concerns. The greatest advantage of this bridge is that it separates vehicles according to their speed, distinguishing them by their speed.

Kansas City Focuses on Road Traffic Safety: The number of vehicle accidents in Kansas City, USA, was quite high last year. The number of people who lost their lives due to vehicle accidents was 100. The number this year should be less, as the number of fatal cases has decreased to two-thirds compared to the same period last year. Currently, the Kansas City police authorities are making every effort to promote road safety campaigns. Police officers riding bicycles are constantly patrolling the main road intersections. Those arrested for drunk driving are either punished with hard labor at the city farm or fined and have their driver's licenses revoked. The laws regarding driver's licenses are also currently under consideration, as the current management of driver's licenses is not as strict as mentioned above.

Decline in Austrian Car Registrations: Among Austria's 600,000 population, there are only 18,870 cars. Comparing cars to the population, there is only one car for every 300 residents. This is according to an estimate by Mr. Stralssen, president of the Austrian Automobile Club. In addition, there are 15,400 trucks, 7,300 taxis, and 51,670 motorcycles. While car registrations are increasing in various European countries, such as Germany with a 20% increase, Austria's car registrations decreased by 39% in 1934. The formation of this situation is largely due to high car taxes.

Morris Car's Long-Distance Driving Performance: Recently, someone signing as MC published an article in the Straits Echo, praising his car trip between Penang and Singapore, proving the economy and durability of the Morris car. The gist is that he bought a Morris Eight car in Penang and drove it for 600 miles. He decided to take a trip to Singapore during the holidays, so he left Bukit Mertajam at 8:45 am on a Saturday morning for Singapore. He did not stop on the way and arrived in Ipoh at 12:00 noon. He left Ipoh at 1:00 pm and arrived in Kuala Lumpur at 6:00 pm. The travel time was seven hours and forty-five minutes, with a gasoline consumption of five and a half gallons and no cylinder oil. The next morning, he departed at 8:00 am and arrived in Singapore at 6:15 pm, which was Sunday evening. The driving time was eight and a half hours, with six gallons of gasoline and no cylinder oil. In addition to him being the driver for the entire trip, there were three other passengers and 100 pounds of luggage. The car drove very well without any obstacles. On the return trip, he took the Malacca route, adding one more passenger and 50 pounds of luggage. He left Singapore at 8:50 am on Tuesday morning and arrived in Muar at 1:00 pm. He continued at 2:30 pm and arrived in Kuala Lumpur at 7:00 pm. The driving time was eight hours and twenty minutes, with a gasoline consumption of six gallons and no cylinder oil. The next morning, he left Kuala Lumpur at 8:00 am, reached Ipoh at 1:00 pm, and returned to Bukit Mertajam at 5:15 pm. The driving time was seven hours and forty-five minutes, with a gasoline consumption of five and a half gallons and no cylinder oil. Throughout the entire round trip, this car had no obstacles and no need for mechanical adjustments, so no repairs were touched. He used the top gear when climbing mountains, except in Menting and Taiping, where he shifted to second gear. He is not boasting, but having driven cars for nearly thirty years, he can honestly say that the 1935 Morris Eight car is the best among small cars. He also thanked Sir Nuffield for the car being equipped with low-pressure tires, providing a stable ride, and using Wakefield oil for lubrication. Before leaving Singapore, the engine casing appeared dry, so he added half a gallon of oil. Although this car traveled 1,300 miles, no half gallon of oil was added to the engine because there was no need. When it reached Bukit Mertajam, the oil level was still full. The gasoline consumption was about 46 miles per gallon, which he thought was very good considering the passengers and luggage on board. Therefore, his advice is "Buy a Morris, no obstacles, and satisfaction guaranteed."

Some Interesting Ford Statistics

(1) The Rouge River Plant in Dearborn, Michigan, covers 1,096 acres. (2) The number of employees at the site once reached as many as 104,000 people. (3) The floor area of the plant totals 7 million square feet. (4) If the windows and skylights of the Rouge River Plant need to be replaced, it would require as much as 330 acres of glass. (5) The ore transporter named "Henry Ford II" carries as much as 12,500 tons of iron ore in one trip. (6) The ore in this ore transporter is unloaded by large unloaders that can lift 12 to 17 tons each time. (7) The huge warehouse (at the Rouge River Plant) can hold as much as 2,000,000 tons of ore, coal, and lime. (8) The railway within the Rouge Plant is 98 miles long. (9) There is an aerial conveyor

Page 26

that is 5 miles long. (10) The amount of water taken from the Detroit River and input into the Ford Plant is 10 million gallons. The amount of water used by the Ford Plant is more than the combined amount used by the three cities of Detroit, Washington, and Cincinnati during the same period. (11) There are 240 coke ovens, producing a total of 3,675 tons of coke, 55 million cubic feet of coal gas, and other valuable by-products every 24 hours. (12) The plant always has "1,200 tons of liquid iron available for immediate needs." (13) Each worker in the Rouge Plant has at least four horsepower of mechanical equipment to assist in their work. All heavy work is done by machinery. The reason why Ford Motor Company can produce inexpensive and high-quality cars is due to the large-scale production indicated by the above points.

Recent Statistics on American Automobile Sales

— Xiao Ang

American automobile sales have dominated the world market for years, but in 1932, the global recession affected the automobile industry, causing it to decline sharply. In recent years, as the world economy has recovered slightly, the automobile industry has also shown signs of recovery. According to expert statistics, the total trade value was US$82,185,100 in 1932, US$93,968,383 in 1933, showing a slight increase, and US$198,314,4855 in 1934, breaking the recent record, but still inferior to the golden age of US$298,652,048 in 1930.

South American countries sell the most passenger cars, as their people are wealthy and the roads are good, mostly cement and asphalt roads, so people are happy to buy cars for transportation. Other countries such as Argentina, Japan, Switzerland, and the United Kingdom also sell a lot. Trucks are sold the most in places like Japan, India, and Australia. Last year, Japan jumped to first place. Trucks are necessary tools in war, and everything from transporting soldiers, food, and weapons relies on them. Japan's purchase of large numbers of trucks reveals its intentions.

New Record for the V8 Ford

Those who are engaged in sea life and desire land adventures are not commonly seen, but Chief Steward Harry Cox, a well-known chief steward on the large Lai Postboat, is an exception. Recently, Mr. Cox in Albany, New York, had urgent business and had to quickly reach Seattle. He personally drove his newly purchased V8 Ford car and traveled 3,240 miles in 60 and a half hours. Although he could not break any speed records set by professional drivers, it is commendable for a non-professional driver to achieve such good results. Moreover, Mr. Cox drove himself throughout this long journey without any help from others. Mr. Cox is quite famous in various parts of the Far East because he not only served as the head of the cooking department for President Coolidge for many years, with excellent results, but is also enthusiastic about wireless electricity and broadcasting activities.
